Anhui Bank Suspends Operations

The Wuhu Anhui Bank opened in the 15th year of the Republic of China, with a capital of 500,000 yuan. It has a branch in Shanghai. The founder, Zhu Jinhou, owned more than half of the shares. He was elected as a director and general manager. Since its opening, the business has been smooth. From the 15th to the 19th year, the profits were quite substantial, so in addition to issuing official dividends, 130,000 yuan was set aside as a public reserve. In the 20th year, the Yangtze River flood caused the decline of commerce in the provinces along the river, and the bank bore the brunt of it, suffering considerable hidden losses. However, it was still able to maintain its operations with great effort. Last year, the bank's General Manager Zhu planned to expand the Shanghai branch's business in order to develop it. In April, he hired Yin Zibai and Hu Shuren to assist in the bank's operations, adding to the number of bonds issued and expanding its dealings. In August, the Wuhu head office suddenly reported a shortage of silver, and the Shanghai branch tried to make adjustments. Later, Jiu Yu Zhuang in Wuhu also lacked silver, and the Shanghai branch indirectly provided relief. Eventually, the Min Rebellion suddenly broke out and could not be repaid for a long time. At that time, Yin and Hu resigned and recommended Chen Yushun to replace them and continue operations until the end of the year. Recently, it was heard that the Shanghai branch, for its own sake, asked the head office to return the amount owed. Unexpectedly, General Manager Zhu suddenly telegraphed the Shanghai branch on the 18th of this month to suspend operations and wait for the shareholders' meeting to be held on March 5 to decide whether to continue. It has been found that the bank has a traffic and real estate bond agreement of 1 million yuan, various deposits of more than 300,000 yuan, and about 500,000 yuan of loans that are difficult to recover. The loans that can be recovered are about 400,000 yuan. After offsetting the deposits and loans and repaying the various deposits, half of the shareholders' capital can still be paid back. The notice is recorded below: Notice is hereby given that this branch has just received a clever telegram from the Wuhu head office stating that since the bank was opened, it has always been prudent. However, since the flood in the 20th year, the transfer of funds for disaster relief to Han and Xun has been stagnant at more than 400,000 yuan. Last year, the Wuhu rice business was just starting, and the Fujian Incident occurred, blocking the Chaozhou and Shantou roads, causing rice merchants to collapse, and the impact was no less than the previous year. Jinhou's service has been inadequate and he feels deeply guilty. The bank's original capital of more than 500,000 yuan has released a book balance of nearly 1 million yuan, and various deposits are only slightly more than 300,000 yuan. However, the book balance cannot be collected immediately, and the deposits cannot be repaid immediately. Considering that his energy is declining, if he does not plan early, it will damage the interests of the depositors, and he will be even more ashamed at that time. Therefore, he requested the board of directors to resolve to seek a liquidation method after the major conclusion on February 13, and to schedule a meeting of all shareholders on March 5 to decide whether to continue. Before the meeting, the collection and settlement will be temporarily suspended. Jinhou is responsible for ensuring that the depositors do not suffer any loss, only a matter of time, and requests understanding. If depositors indicate the debts of the bank's debtors and both parties agree, the bank can transfer the accounts at any time to reduce the scope. Please check and handle accordingly. It has been found that the Shanghai branch has released a book balance of more than 500,000 yuan and various deposits of 220,000 yuan, which is more than enough to offset the two. Now, according to the telegram from the head office, the collection and payment will be temporarily suspended, pending the decision of the general meeting of shareholders on March 5. This is a reasonable notice, and we hope for public understanding. February 19th, 23rd year of the Republic of China.

The Two-Roads Council Makes Demands

Representatives are appointed to petition the Railway Bureau.

The Railway Bureau has responded to each item.

The Council of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Workers' Union, based on the talks of the representatives of the branch offices on February 2, resolved to demand that the Railway Bureau promptly announce the annual salary increase, performance appraisal methods, and other regulations. It specially appointed directors Min Luo-ying, Chen Bohua, Feng Qishu, and others as representatives to petition the Railway Bureau. It is now known that the Railway Bureau has made a reply to each item. The reporter of the New News Agency has specially explored and recorded the situation, which is recorded as follows:

Petition

The association's petition to the Railway Bureau stated, "Petition for petition matters. This association is for the sake of rectifying association affairs, promoting work to develop the railway industry, and advocating equal treatment. Therefore, it convened a meeting of representatives of branch offices on February 2. After the association affairs and other items were discussed, many cases were submitted by the branch offices. As a result of the discussions, it was decided that the association's directors Min Luo-ying, Chen Bohua, Feng Qishu, Wang Weixia, Xue Jie, Cai Jinghai, Yuan Qichang, and other directors will lead all the representatives (a list is attached) to the bureau to petition at 9:00 a.m. today. Please examine and approve them separately, and sincerely reply to each case (the reasons for the cases are attached separately). The matter concerns the welfare of all employees of the two roads. The time for the petition is imminent.

Nine Demands

The association has made nine demands to the Railway Bureau, which are recorded as follows: (1) The request for the annual salary increase for employees in the second half of the 22nd year should be promptly announced. (2) The request for the prompt announcement of the annual salary increase and performance appraisal methods, as well as other regulations. (3) The request to negotiate with the Railway Bureau to allow branch offices to send official telegrams. (4) For car service employees who work on national holidays, they should be given one day of substitute leave pay in accordance with the Employee Service Regulations. (5) For low-level workers in the car service, mechanical service, and public works departments, the salary should be increased to the same level as the workers in the materials department. (6) Employees who are promoted should receive a promotion salary increase, which should not affect the annual salary increase. (7) Director Mo Heng of the General Affairs Department has slandered the Party and the country, destroyed the labor movement, and engaged in private fraud. Most of the matters have not been determined. Please provide a solution. (8) It is often difficult for workers to ask for leave of absence from the factory. Compared with the implementation situation of the Wusong Machine Factory, the treatment is very unfair. The old system before August of the 20th year should be restored. (9) Employee family members' free tickets and benefit tickets must be issued locally.

Railway Bureau's Reply

The original text of the reply from the Two-Roads Administration states, "All submitted documents have been noted. The following are the instructions for each case: (1) The performance appraisal and salary increase case for the second half of the 22nd year is being rushed and will be announced and submitted to the ministry for approval soon. (2) The performance appraisal and salary increase methods are being reviewed and formulated. Before the announcement, all performance appraisal matters are handled in accordance with the regulations of the ministry and the customs of this road that do not conflict with the regulations of the ministry. The ministry's instructions on the performance appraisal and salary increase method have been announced many times and do not need to be announced again. (3) The branch offices of the association may send telegrams if they are necessary for official business, but they must be signed by the stationmaster before they can be sent. It should also be noted that the branch offices of the labor union must not directly publish documents and telegrams to the outside world. (4) On December 8 of the 20th year, this bureau promulgated the regulations for the payment of overtime work salaries in various departments, stipulating that rotating workers shall not receive overtime work or holiday work salaries. Previously, the association forwarded requests from the Shanghai-Hangzhou and Yongshao sections to add holiday work salaries to the car service station team employees. After the car service department's investigation and reply, the employees are all rotating workers and cannot be given salary increases in accordance with the previous regulations. Article 10 of the Employee Service Regulations refers to those who exceed their designated service time, and Article 11 refers to those who are assigned to work overtime during holidays by the主管人员. Those who were originally scheduled to work on holidays and did not exceed the stipulated time shall not cite the above regulations. However, whether the commemorative holidays stipulated by the National Government should be handled in the same way as ordinary holidays should be reported to the ministry for instructions. (5) The expansion of the salary range for workers in the Materials Department was originally because the treatment of workers in that department was lower than that of other departments. The wages of workers in various departments who are below 24 yuan, such as road maintenance crews in the public works department, porters in the car service department, and car wipers in the mechanical service department, either have dormitories, uniforms, or temporary allowances. The treatment is already better, and there are opportunities for promotion and transfer. The original treatment of workers in the Materials Department was meager, and there was no hope for promotion or transfer. Therefore, after detailed consultation with the Party Department and the labor union, they were allowed to expand the salary range to show fairness. Workers in various departments should not request this example again. (6) Employees who have served less than one year after a promotion cannot be evaluated for salary increases, which is clearly stipulated by the ministry. The request conflicts with the ministry's regulations and should not be approved. (7) Please wait for the ministry's instructions to resolve it. (8) The original submission is unclear and has been ordered to be investigated and handled by the mechanical service department. (9) If employees and their families are unable to obtain free train tickets from the railway bureau due to emergencies, the主管首领 of the factory section may issue them locally. This bureau has already issued a circular to all departments to comply with it. The request should not be discussed. Let it be known. This order."

River Transport Companies in Sichuan Seek to Save Shipping Industry

丨Cooperation Alliance Agreed Yesterday Afternoon丨

Cotton Yarn Freight Rises by Ten Yuan

All Cargo Freight Rates Increased

The route from Shanghai to Chongqing, Sichuan, has always been transferred from Yichang to Chongqing by river boats. Since the opening of direct Shanghai-Chongqing routes by Minsheng, Taikang, Taikoo, Jardine, and other shipping companies in recent years, freight rates have plummeted. The river route in Sichuan, which the shipping industry once regarded as a golden route, was almost like chicken ribs last year. With short freight rates and a lack of cargo, excessive competition has led to a situation where income cannot cover expenditure, resulting in great losses for all companies. Now, in order to save the river transport industry in Sichuan, the shipping companies have decided to abandon the past competition and adopt the principle of alliance and cooperation, so that the companies can unite and raise freight rates. A meeting was held in Shanghai last night to determine the direction of cooperation. This reporter believes that this matter has a great impact on the Yangtze River shipping industry, and has made a special trip to various parties for a thorough investigation, and the general situation is recorded as follows:

Low Freight Rates and Losses for Shipping Companies

The cargo shipped from Shanghai to Sichuan is mainly cotton yarn. In the past, when freight rates were at their highest, each piece of cotton yarn shipped to Chongqing would cost more than 30 taels of silver. This was still the price for transferring via Yichang. In recent years, since the shipping companies added direct Shanghai-Chongqing ships, the ships only cared about loading cargo and did not consider costs. Last year, prices fell repeatedly. In the shortest time, each piece of cotton yarn only cost 8 yuan, and even in the shallow water period, it only cost 12 yuan, which is equivalent to just over 8 taels and 5 qian of silver, which is not enough to cover the cost of each ship's operation. Due to the drop in cotton yarn prices, other goods also fell along with it. Last year, none of the river boats in Sichuan were able to make a profit, and almost all of them suffered losses.

Agreement to Save Alliance Cooperation

Currently, there are Taikoo, Jardine, Jiejiang, Sanbei, Minsheng, Guangyao, China Merchants, and other companies operating river boats in Shanghai. At the beginning of this month, British companies such as Taikoo, in view of the constant price reduction and competition of river boats in Sichuan, the result of which would be mutual destruction and unnecessary sacrifices, negotiated with Chinese companies such as Minsheng and Chuanbei to save the river transport industry in Sichuan. The first step was to eliminate competition among companies and realize alliance cooperation. Referring to the precedent of the four companies in the Shanghai-Ningbo route, all river boats would jointly operate, redetermine the freight rates for various goods, abide by the alliance regulations, and not have any private price increases or decreases. The cargo delivery forms of each company must be exchanged and viewed. This measure has been unanimously approved by all companies.

Open Methods of Yesterday Afternoon's Meeting

Taikoo, Jardine, Minsheng, Jiejiang, Sanbei, and others each sent representatives to gather at the Jiejiang Company on the Bund at 4:00 p.m. yesterday to publicly discuss the open methods of alliance cooperation for river boats in Sichuan. Guangyao Company was also invited to join. It was heard that the Chinese side had several opinions, such as Gaoxian and Yibu, where British ships have not yet been able to navigate. The goods loaded on Chinese ships in that port should not be included in the cooperation conditions. In addition, the section from Kuizhou to Wushan should be operated by Chinese ships. Mail and other shipments should be carried by each ship and not be included in public distribution. If there are troop transports, Chinese ships should provide the service, but the business during that period should also be distributed publicly. These are the proposals made by the Chinese shipping companies. Otherwise, they can all abide by the agreed methods.

Increase Freight Rates and Redetermine Transport Rates

After the cooperative principles of the shipping companies were passed, they continued to discuss the increase in freight rates on the Sichuan River. The current freight rates are not enough to cover costs and losses are worrying. The main cargo transported from Shanghai to Sichuan is cotton yarn, so the cotton yarn freight rate will be used as a target. Currently, the price of each piece of cotton yarn from Shanghai to Chongqing is 12 yuan. Now, it is publicly agreed to increase it by 10 yuan, and the freight rate for each piece is increased to 22 yuan. According to the original rate, it is increased by about 80%. The freight rates for other miscellaneous goods are also increased by 70% to 80% in proportion to the cotton yarn freight rate. The detailed tariff (i.e., freight rate list) for the detailed goods will be discussed and redetermined by the representatives of each company, and then the new prices will be announced and implemented. The representatives unanimously passed the proposal at the time.

Customs Brokers' Association Also Holds Meeting

When the Sichuan customs brokers heard this news, they thought that since the river shipping industry in Sichuan had changed its current system, allied and cooperated, and increased freight rates, this move was also closely related to the customs brokers. Therefore, all Sichuan customs brokers were convened by the Customs Brokers' Association yesterday for an emergency meeting at the Customs Brokers' Association to discuss the contact with customers after accepting the new freight rates and new methods of the shipping companies. As for the alliance and cooperation of the shipping companies, after the draft methods are determined and the transport rates are announced, they must be jointly implemented within this month.

Existing Chinese and Foreign Shipping Companies on the Sichuan River

Currently, the commercial ships sailing on the Sichuan River from Shanghai to Chongqing include four ships from Jiejiang Company, four ships from Minsheng Company, three ships each from Taikoo and Jardine, two ships from Sanbei Company (Fuhua and Fuyang), and one ship from China Merchants Bureau, which is currently stranded. There are also six ships from Guangyao Company. The above are all direct Shanghai-Chongqing lines. There are also more than ten ships from Jiejiang, Minsheng, Taikoo, Jardine, etc. on the Shanghai-Yichang route.

Court to Send Forensic Doctor to Examine Li Guojie's Condition

No News Yet from the Supreme Court's Judgment

Li Guojie, the former general manager of the China Merchants Steamship Bureau, was sentenced to three years in prison by the Shanghai District Court for privately borrowing foreign debts and engaging in bribery. Chen Fumu and Wang Yunzhang, who were on the run, were also wanted. Li refused to accept the judgment and appealed. After the High Court summoned him for trial, the sentence was changed to three years and six months. After Li was sent to the court, he was sent to Shanghai Hospital for accommodation because he had a long-term illness and could not be detained for long. The Fuchang Ginseng Bank and lawyer Jiang Yiping reported to the court, which ordered him to be sent to Shanghai Hospital for accommodation, and multiple police officers were sent to take turns to protect him. His life was still comfortable. However, Li again declared that he was dissatisfied and appealed to the Supreme Court, the court of final instance. There has been no news of the judgment to date. The District Court has paid close attention to Li's case, and the reception of guests and the entry and exit of letters are closely monitored. Moreover, Li has been hospitalized for treatment for one year. It is not known whether he has recovered, so it is planned to send a forensic doctor to the hospital to examine him to clarify the truth.

Two Kidnappers in Tao Changhai Case Sentenced to Death

The Other Bandits Were Given Heavy Sentences

Tao Changhai, a local compradore of the Ellis Foreign Company on North Sichuan Road, returned to Shanghai from Hangzhou on his own car at 11:00 p.m. on December 24th last year. While traveling near North Henan Road and Laobazi Road, he was kidnapped by bandits and hidden in a foreign house at No. 9 Beihai Road. After the case of extortion was reported, it was solved by Chief Inspector Lu Liankui of the Investigation Division of the General Patrol Room, Detective Liu Shaokui, and Chinese and Western detectives. The hostage Tao Changhai was rescued, and nine men and women, including the kidnappers Fei Xiangqing, Xu Arong, Xu Zhaofu, Zhou Songlin, Zhang Linsheng, and Chen Dequan, were arrested and sent to the First Special District Local Court. It was also found that Xu Arong had colluded with the escaped Wu Zicheng, Tao Yutang, Zhang Xiaobai, Su Zicai, etc., at noon on July 21 of the 19th year of the Republic of China to kidnap Xie Keming, the former compradore of Ellis Foreign Company, near Jiangxi Road and Sijing Road, and hide him at No. 12 Yidingpan Road in the French Concession, and extorted a large sum of money. Later, the family members redeemed the ticket with 15,000 yuan. Fei Xiangqing, Xu Arong, Xu Zhaofu, Zhou Songlin, Lu Jinbao, Tao Yutang, and Chen Guisheng, who were sentenced to death by the Second Special Court, kidnapped Wu Wuxing, the manager of a company, on Baek Road at 8:00 a.m. on February 25th of the year before last and hid him in the house at No. 13 Laodeng Road in the French Concession, and extorted a large sum of money. Later, the family members also redeemed the ticket with 25,000 yuan. The details of the interrogation have been repeatedly recorded in this newspaper. Upon instruction, the discussion was concluded and the sentence was awaited. Yesterday morning, Judge Liu Yugui visited the Third Criminal Court and sentenced Fei Xiangqing and Xu Arong to death. Xu Zhaofu and Zhou Songlin were each sentenced to sixteen years of imprisonment. Zhang Linsheng was sentenced to fifteen years of imprisonment, and Chen Dequan was sentenced to six years. The number of days of detention before the determination of the judgment shall be offset by one day of imprisonment for every two days. Three pistols, sixty-six bullets, and various exhibits shall be confiscated according to the list. Zhu Kunshan, Fei Zhu's, and Xu Xue's were all found not guilty. The bureau's lawyer, Wang Yaotang, requested that he be detained during the appeal period, and the court approved it.

More Than 100 Shops on Dayang Bridge in Zhabei Present to Railway Bureau for Exemption from Demolishing Bridge

To Maintain Business on the Opposite Bank

More than 100 shops such as Hesheng Rice Store and Sauce Garden on Dayang Bridge in Zhabei presented a petition to the two railways yesterday to stop the demolition of the wooden bridge in order to facilitate transportation. The original petition stated, "Petition to preserve the necessary road to maintain the commercial market, and to request that the matter be examined and approved to show compassion for the merchants. Since Dayang Bridge and the Panjiawan area were destroyed in the disaster of January 28, the losses have been almost complete. However, they have been forced to make a living and have worked hard to resume business. Fortunately, there is a wooden bridge that crosses the railway at the east end of Dayang Bridge, which can be used to communicate with the citizens of Panjiawan. About 20,000 people come and go every day, which is beneficial to merchants and convenient for workers. They trade with each other to maintain their livelihoods. Now, a concrete wall is being built along the railway, and there is talk of demolishing the wooden bridge to prevent traffic. If it is implemented, it will be inconvenient for the citizens of both sides to travel, and the commercial and industrial markets will be greatly affected. The disadvantages of factories and the closure of shops are foreseeable. It is inevitable that they will be affected by the disaster. Merchants and people have no way to make a living and no place to rely on. Although it is a small road problem, how can the magnitude of its relationship be overstated? It is hereby jointly petitioned to the bureau to show compassion for the people's difficulties, preserve the necessary road, and maintain the commercial market, which is truly virtuous (omitted below)."

And Entrusts Master Yuan Ying to Come to Shanghai as a Representative to Beg for Relief

The Shanghai Xinwei Relief Association received a letter from the Fujian Provincial Buddhist Association yesterday, stating that since the rebellion occurred in the province, many Buddhist temples in various places have been burned and robbed, and monks and lay refugees are living in the open air, which is extremely tragic. The most serious cases include the Xuefeng Chong Sheng Temple in the provincial capital, which was robbed by rebellious soldiers, and the Jile Temple in Gutian, which was destroyed. The temples, dharma objects, and Buddha statues were lost in the amount of tens of thousands of yuan. The Wenhua Temple in Luoyuan was also burned. The Zhong Cui Temple in Yanping was looted, and the monks were looted and the artifacts were scattered. The Qisheng and Bailin Temples in Xiapu were shot and killed by bandits, suffering heavy losses. The vast disasters have occurred and there is no way to appeal. The compatriots who have suffered disasters are also urgently awaiting relief. Our colleagues are weak and think repeatedly. The only thing we can do is to rely on philanthropists at home and abroad to develop great compassion, relieve the immediate crisis, allocate funds to help, and relieve the suffering of all beings. We hereby entrust Master Yuan Ying to sincerely request the gentlemen of your association to consider the severe military disaster in Fujian Province and quickly allocate funds to assist in disaster relief. The monks and lay people will be very grateful. If you would like to give instructions, please hand them over to Master Yuan Ying for collection and remittance to Fujian for distribution. With best wishes for your health and well-being, and hoping for a reply."

Anyone Who Has Been Introduced and Proven Can Participate

Plans to Set Up a Store and a Snow Shame Soap Factory

Former Northeast Anti-Japanese Army Major General Jiang Minsheng has recently found that shining shoes and selling domestic goods in Shanghai can help himself and others. The charter is recorded below:

Charter of the Group

(1) Name: Northeast Refugee Life Self-Help Group, (2) Purpose: To seek fundamental relief for refugees and anti-Japanese comrades, to cultivate the spirit of self-help, self-reliance, and self-sufficiency, and to achieve recovery.

Sentencing of Zhou Zhanyuan, Manager of the New-New Company, to Life Imprisonment for Shooting

Zhou's Wife and Two Sons Kneel, Begging for the Release of Funds Owed by New-New

Zhou Zhanyuan, a Tianjin native and the head watchman for the New-New Company, shot and killed Li Minzhou, the company's general manager, in room 327 of the New-New Hotel on the 1st of this month after Li repeatedly refused Zhou's requests to resign. Detectives Huang Yingjie and Liu Xianglun of the police arrested Zhou. Li Zhishan, the police lawyer, prosecuted him under Article 284 of the criminal law for premeditated murder. The First Special Court has concluded its interrogation, and yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shide of the Criminal Division presided over the First Criminal Court and pronounced the verdict: Zhou Zhanyuan is sentenced to life imprisonment for murder, and the pistol is confiscated. After the verdict, Zhou's wife and two children knelt before the court, stating that the funds Zhou was owed by the New-New Company had not been paid, despite repeated requests. Even when the court previously instructed Lawyer Wei to retrieve the funds, they were not obtained. They pleaded for relief. The court stated that the funds owed by New-New should rightfully be paid and ordered Lawyer Wei to retrieve them again.

Furthermore, the New-New Company sent a letter stating, "Our company's former general manager, Mr. Li Minzhou, died in the line of duty, and your newspaper has reported on this matter repeatedly. However, regarding the repeated requests by the perpetrator Zhou Zhanyuan in court to be paid his salary, we must make a careful clarification. After investigation, the perpetrator has already received and signed for all salary due to him. What he is now demanding is the wooden box bonus. This bonus does not belong to the company; it is public funds accumulated by all employed shareholders and distributed to employees who have been dedicated in their duties at the end of each year as an incentive. Since the perpetrator expressed his demand for the bonus, our company's management has received a signed letter from all employed shareholders, stating that they vow never to give the bonus to such a heinous murderer. Therefore, our company cannot grant the payment. We hope your newspaper will report the truth accurately. New-New Co., Ltd. respectfully."

Charter of the Northeast Youth Lost Territory Recovery Corps

The purpose of this corps is to recover lost territories. (3) Qualifications: All compatriots and anti-Japanese comrades who embrace the determination to resist Japan, save the country, and vow to recover lost territories, and who have a reliable letter of introduction proving their identity, may participate. (4) Organization: The corps will have one general director, one secretary, two chief officers, and several officers. (5) Powers: The general director will manage all affairs of the corps. Other staff members shall obey the guidance of the general director and assist in all work of the corps. (6) Meetings: The corps' executive committee will meet once a week. All resolutions will be submitted to the general director for execution. (7) Treatment: All members of the corps will receive equal treatment in terms of living conditions. (8) Production: The first step of the corps will be to focus on production by shining shoes and selling domestic goods in the city. The second step will be to establish a Northeast Refugee Domestic Goods Store and a Northeast National Humiliation Soap Factory to concentrate production and economic talents. The third step will be to establish branches in various regions to help our compatriots and cultivate a spirit of self-reliance. Other productive enterprises will be implemented gradually. (9) Economy: The corps' economy will be based entirely on exchanging labor for resources, without soliciting donations, issuing shares, or receiving any subsidies. (10) Members: The members of the corps must stand on the basis of self-reliance, self-sufficiency, enduring pain while waiting for the right time, and vowing to recover lost territories. The general director bears the divine duty of saving the nation and will strive for national salvation. Members of other political parties are not allowed to participate; otherwise, they will be warned, and if they do not listen, they will be expelled immediately. (11) Surplus: Thirty percent of the corps' surplus will be used as the corps' construction fund, 20 percent will be used for student scholarships, 20 percent will be used for temporary relief for compatriots, and 30 percent will be used for the remuneration of members. (A separate charter for the distribution of labor remuneration will be established.) (12) Addendum: This charter will be implemented from the date of promulgation.

We hope to receive your guidance on all matters in the future. Respectfully submitted to the United Association for Relief of Northeast Refugees.

Controversy Over the Natural Science Textbook Published by Datong Bookstore

In the "Sending a Telegram to Beiping" lesson on page 41 of the seventh volume of the New Life Natural Science Textbook published by the Datong Bookstore in Shanghai, it states that a telegram from Shanghai to Beiping must pass through several telegraph offices in Nanjing, Tianjin, and others, and it usually takes one or two days to arrive. The editor lacks knowledge of telecommunications and is completely inconsistent with the facts, arousing public anger among telegraph office personnel across the country. They have successively petitioned the Ministry of Communications to request the Ministry of Education to order corrections. At the same time, they have also requested the National Telegraph Workers' Welfare Association to engage a lawyer to negotiate with the Datong Bookstore. The Datong Bookstore replied to the Ministry of Communications and the lawyer that it had complied with the Ministry's order to make corrections, and all existing books have been revised, and the original version has long been discontinued. However, in reality, the bookstore is still selling the original version in stock. The Telegraph Workers' Welfare Association recently purchased the book from the bookstore multiple times, and it was always the original version and had not been replaced. The association, fearing that the bookstore would deny it, sent staff to the Datong Bookstore on Fuzhou Road on the 10th of this month to purchase four copies, which were still the old version. The association believed that the Datong Bookstore was deliberately deceiving and making malicious publicity, so they immediately asked the Chinese police to certify it and reported it to the police station. At the same time, they also asked a third party, Mr. Xu, to be present to certify that the more than 50 textbooks stored in the cabinet were all original versions, in order to prevent denial. It is reported that the association has reported the matter to the Ministry of Communications and requested the lawyer to negotiate with the Datong Bookstore again.

Another Voice for Rent Reduction

Organization of a Rent Reduction Branch in Sanduo Lane

The houses in Sanduo Lane, Daji Road, Nanshi, are managed by Liyi Real Estate Company. On the 31st of last month, the tenants of the lane stated that Daji Road is not a prosperous area, and the houses are not spacious or well-built, but the rent for each house is 32 yuan per month. Adding water, electricity, and housing taxes, the monthly burden is more than 40 yuan, which is truly unbearable. Moreover, the houses in the area were hastily constructed due to careless construction, and the walls are damp, and water drips down, damaging clothing. Electricity and running water were delayed for many days before being installed. Therefore, they jointly sent a letter to the company requesting a fair rent reduction and a delay in the rent start date by half a month. Nearly two weeks have passed, but the company has not responded. The tenants held an ad hoc meeting on the 16th, with 38 households participating. Zhang Longhai was elected chairman, and Fang Weiren from the Municipal Party Department attended and gave guidance. It was immediately resolved to organize the Shanghai Rent Reduction Committee, Daji Road Sanduo Lane Branch, in the Hunan District of Shanghai. Zhang Longhai, Tang Shuming, Qian Yichai, Shen Xiaochu, and Li Qilin were elected as committee members to join the general association and strive to carry out the rent reduction movement until the goal is achieved. It was also stipulated that the monthly rent amount should be deposited in the Ximen Branch of the Shanghai Bank and paid after the landlord's satisfactory response. The association also invited lawyers Mei Hezhang, Wang Chengkuan, and Huang Daping as legal advisors.

Wen Zongyao is Innocent

A Dispute Over Concubinage Comes to an End

Wen Zongyao, who was appointed as a president during the era of the seven presidents of the Southwest Military Government, still entered the world of romance in his old age. Two years ago, he took the prostitute Shouzhen (i.e., Jin Yuan) as his concubine and used the three-story attic at 584 Tiantong Road as her golden house. While Wen was reporting the case to the police for investigation, a widow from Hangzhou, Yu Wang, claimed to be Jin Yuan's mother and accused Wen of kidnapping at the First Special District Court. The trial has concluded, and the announcement of the verdict was pending, as reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon was the date for the verdict in the case. The defendant Wen Zongyao still went to the court with his lawyer, but the plaintiff did not appear in court. Judge Wu Zehan then took the seat in the Second Court and announced the verdict. The main text stated that the defendant Wen Zongyao was not guilty. The counter-suit filed by Wen against Yu Wang for false accusation was also dismissed at the same time.

Blind Elder Brother Sues Younger Brother for Abandonment

Zhu Binzhang, the owner of the Mingfeng Organ Factory at 1 Ciji Lane, Gonghexin Road, Zhabei, is from Zhenhai, Zhejiang. In 1931, because his elder brother Zhu Linzhang repeatedly pestered him, he sued in the local court, requesting to sever the brotherly relationship. The court advised Zhu Binzhang to provide Zhu Linzhang, who was blind and unable to support himself, with 20 yuan per month for living expenses. Zhu Binzhang listened to the advice and, out of brotherly affection, agreed to do so. However, Zhu Linzhang demanded 10,000 yuan for living expenses, which led to litigation that has lasted for more than two years and remains unresolved. Recently, Zhu Linzhang hired a lawyer to publish a statement, claiming that the Mingfeng Organ Factory was established with the joint investment of him and his younger brother Zhu Binzhang, and filed a lawsuit with the procuratorate of the local court, accusing his younger brother Zhu Binzhang of abandoning him. Zhu Binzhang also published a rebuttal in the newspaper and submitted a statement to the court, stating that Binzhang's father died when he was three years old, and because there was no inheritance, he was raised by his maternal grandparents. Before he reached adulthood, he came to Shanghai to work and became a craftsman in the Science Instrument Museum. Later, he and his friends Wang Rongchu and Lin Zhangfu jointly established the Mingfeng Organ Factory in 1915. Zhu Linzhang did not invest any money in it. At that time, Linzhang also independently established the Zhu Yongtai Woodworking Business, and they each lived separately with independent economies. In 1918, Wang Rongchu and Lin Zhangfu were unwilling to continue the business and handed it over to Binzhang to operate solely. When their father passed away, he left behind more than one mu of paddy fields and two and a half tiled houses, which have not been divided, and Binzhang has not occupied them. In 1931, there was a lawsuit in your court. At that time, Linzhang proposed to divide the organ factory. Binzhang refused because Zhu Linzhang had no investment in the factory. The judge repeatedly advised him to give him 20 yuan per month for living expenses, but he was dissatisfied, and there was no result. There was no intention to abandon, nor was there any act of abandonment, so he should not be held criminally responsible for abandonment. The day before yesterday, Prosecutor Tang Ruxiu ordered both parties to appear in court. As a result of the interrogation, they were instructed to reconcile out of court. It is said that there is no possibility of reconciliation in this case. Yesterday, the judge issued another order for both parties to appear in court, scheduled to continue the interrogation and decision today.

Training Sea Lions at Bansong Garden

Starting from the 14th of this month (the first day of the abolished lunar new year), Mr. and Mrs. Dai Gejun, sea lion performance experts from the Shanghai-Haijingbo Circus Troupe, are training sea lions in the Four Sides Hall of the Garden. The various strange shapes and actions are very interesting. However, the sea lions are naturally fierce and difficult to train. Fortunately, Mr. and Mrs. Dai Gejun have worked hard to train them, and the sea lions can now perform a variety of tricks, such as rolling a ball on their noses and other skills. Therefore, there have been many tourists in the garden in recent days, marveling at the sight. We hope that people do not miss this opportunity.

De'an Steamer Capsizes Manure Boat

Four-Year-Old Child Drowned

Tang Lishan, a manure boat owner from Yancheng, recently loaded fertilizer worth 30 yuan from the Suzhou River and sailed eastward along the Pudong side. When he arrived outside the Hongsheng Wharf near the Liyi Ferry, the Taikoo Steamship Company's De'an steamer was raising anchor to exit and was turning around in that location. The vessels were unable to avoid each other in time, and the De'an steamer struck the manure boat violently in the middle of its port side. The manure boat was immediately overturned, and filth flowed everywhere, with a stench filling the air. There were Tang and his wife, one older child, and five younger children on board, who all fell into the river. After the accident, nearby boats rushed to the rescue, and seven people were rescued. However, Tang's four-year-old son, named Xiao Liuzi, was originally tied with a rope around his waist to prevent him from falling into the river. When the boat capsized, Xiao Liuzi fell into the water and the rope came loose, and he sank and disappeared, tragically drowning. The capsized boat floated with the tide to the surface of Zhangjiabang Creek on the south side, where it was recovered by others. Afterward, the Chinese police of the Maritime Customs Water Police Station took the rescued seven people to the police station. However, Tang's two-year-old daughter, Sheng Nü, became unconscious due to drinking too much water, and Tang himself was stabbed in the lower left ear by a boat hook during the rescue. Therefore, the police sent the two to Renji Hospital. Fortunately, Tang's daughter gradually recovered, and Tang's injuries were not serious. Yesterday, the father and daughter were discharged from the hospital. The police have instructed Tang to submit a petition to the Maritime Customs Port Authority, requesting that the Taikoo Company compensate for the loss of the boat and cargo and provide compensation for the victim.

Railway Department Stipulates Fees for Ferrying Mail Cars Across the River

Instructs Railway Bureau to Comply Yesterday

The Two-Way Railway Administration received instructions from the Ministry of Railways yesterday, stating that the Jinpu Railway stated that the Union Transport Office stated that the mail cars attached to the trains are calculated according to volume, at a rate of one cent per cubic meter per kilometer. Regarding the Shanghai-Beiping trains 1201 and 1202, after direct access to the capital ferry, all such mail cars should take Tianjin East Station to Nanjing as the starting and ending points. The Ministry had previously stipulated that the capital ferry distance across the river was ten kilometers. It is requested that the office be consulted as to whether the mail cars should calculate an additional ten kilometers for the capital ferry between Tianjin East Station and Pukou. In response, the Ministry has now stipulated that the fee for mail cars passing through the capital ferry across the river should be determined with reference to the provisions of Article 114 of the Union Transport Regulations for public parcels, at half the rate of ordinary parcel freight. After deducting half, the fee for mail cars passing through the river shall be based on the actual volume given to each mail car. The ordinary parcel passing fee is determined by Order No. 6853 of the Industry Department, collecting three cents per kilogram. The half fee for mail cars passing through the river should be one and a half cents per kilogram. The method of converting cubic meters to kilograms should be based on the provisions of Article 26 of the Freight Car Regulations, converting three cubic meters to one metric ton and one metric ton to one thousand kilograms, collecting one and a half cents per kilogram passing fee. For clarity, a calculation formula for calculating the mail car crossing fee is attached, and it is required to comply and handle the matter. The bureau has instructed the Transportation Department to comply.

Garrison Command Justifiably Refuses

Yong'an Hall Prosecutes a Counterfeit Wanjinyou Case in Tainan

The Tiger Balm Wanjinyou created by Yong'an Hall has effective medicinal properties and sells extremely well. As a result, a group of unscrupulous merchants and profiteers, disregarding human well-being, spare no effort to use counterfeit and imitative tricks. Cases of this kind have been discovered in the motherland and various parts of Southeast Asia, and the situations of the hall sending people to arrest and prosecute those involved are often reported. It has just been learned that Lu Jueshen, the special investigator of the hall in Taiwan, sent a report yesterday on the seizure of counterfeit medicine, stating that at the beginning of this month, he learned that counterfeit Tiger Balm Wanjinyou was being sold in Tainan. He immediately tried to buy it and requested the Tainan authorities to handle the case fairly. The governor of the prefecture personally led him to the head of the health department's home, then to the director's office of the judicial affairs, presenting a dozen fake Wanjinyou and nine purchase orders for review. On the 9th of this month, they carefully investigated the printing of the fake medicine and the manufacturing location of the empty bottles. They went to the addresses of the three parties and the name of the counterfeiter, who turned out to be Chen Youcai, located at 49 Yongle Town 3-chome, Tainan. They reported to the police station, informing them of the address of the counterfeiter. At 4 pm, judicial director Wu Tianjiri led several bailiffs to surround Chen Youcai's residence. Chen was caught off guard and 50 cans of counterfeit Wanjinyou and correspondence were found. Chen Youcai was immediately detained. Later, the judicial director searched Chen Youcai's house again and found a large amount of counterfeit medicine materials, which are currently being investigated. After more arrests are made, they will be jointly prosecuted and punished according to the law.

Four Banks Joint Treasury Issues Reserve Report

Number 215

The Four Banks Joint Treasury, jointly established by the Yien Yieh, Kincheng, China & South Sea, and Continental Banks, specializes in issuing banknotes for the China & South Sea Bank. In accordance with the Treasury's issuance regulations, banknote issuance is backed by full reserves. Cash reserves must be at least 60%, and guarantee reserves must be at most 40%. A public announcement is made weekly, and the announcement is audited by auditors and accountants from the four banks. The 215th public announcement of the Shanghai Reserve of February 10th, Year 23, is recorded below. The total value of banknotes in circulation is 28,685,037 yuan. The total value of reserves is 28,685,037 yuan, including 12,282,787 yuan in cash reserves and 6,400,125 yuan in guarantee reserves.

Reading Guidance:

"What kind of talent is needed in today's society?" Perhaps no one can give a concrete answer to this question? In this flood of unemployment, it can be said that there is a surplus of all kinds of talent, and none is needed. But when we think of the underdevelopment of China's industries, and when we think of the day when we will talk about construction, we will feel that there is not enough of any kind of talent, and all are needed. We are indeed trapped in this contradiction now. This is probably an inevitable phenomenon in China during this transition period!

In "Reading Q&A," we have repeatedly pointed out that an individual's "path" should be compatible with society's "path," otherwise you will only have illusions and disappointments, and you will not achieve a true "path." To study for the sake of a "path" is naturally the most correct method. But you must never only look at yourself with his eyes, regardless of society. You say: "I read to survive." If the "survival" you speak of means coexisting and prospering with society, this is correct; if it is only for the temporary selfish survival of one person, then "reading" is not only meaningless, but also unable to achieve the goal.

Since the purpose of reading cannot be limited to one's own personal selfishness, the choice of learning paths should not be limited to one's own preferences. At the very least, personal interests can only be placed in a secondary position and cannot but be given special attention.

There is a big contradiction in your letter. On the one hand, you sing the praises of "reading to increase survival skills," but what have you chosen? It is "poetry," which cannot be used to make a living, and it is the literary antique of China's past. According to you, it is to "express the feelings in your heart," this purpose has obviously changed.

We do not oppose readers freely choosing subjects to study. We originally only stood on the sidelines and offered some guidance and advice. If you want to study literature, although we cannot guarantee that you will not be disappointed, since your purpose is "to increase survival skills," this is indeed a path. According to the needs of society, it cannot be said that a certain era can do without literature. However, what you have chosen is the antique of the past, the "elegant" profession that only those with ample time and affluent lives can engage in. Now there are only a few "old relics" and "young masters" left who use this kind of style to "express the feelings in their hearts."

Needless to say, this choice is harmful to people like you.

Probably because you "stay at home all day and are very alienated from everything in society!" You are indeed too vague about real life. We feel that people living in an environment like yours should read more books to understand real society. Even if you read literature, you should naturally read modern works, and you should not go back to chewing on antiques. Vernacular poetry has long been harvested in China, and there are many famous works worth reading. Vernacular expression is also freer than classical Chinese, the dead sounds have long been liberated, now natural sounds are used, modern sounds are used, and there is no need for "poetry rhymes" and other rubbish.

Therefore, from our assessment of you, it is okay for you to study some poetry in your spare time, but please study vernacular poetry first. At the same time, we also hope that you do not forget reality. You must know that the people who will be able to survive in the future society must be people with new knowledge, correct understanding, organized minds, able to adapt to group life, and have the perseverance to never give up.

Chunqiu

The Solitary Garden

— Yan Qiao

Mencius said that solitary enjoyment is not as good as shared enjoyment. This is the most high-sounding statement. Therefore, those autocratic tyrants who cover up their peaceful facade must display the banner of "sharing joy with the people" so that the common people will obediently swallow their tears and shout "Long live the emperor!"

But Sima was dishonest and impolite, naming his villa "Solitary Garden." Mr. Tai once scolded him at a certain lecture, saying that he was far inferior to Fan Zhongyan, who was concerned about the world's troubles before anyone else and rejoiced only after everyone else had enjoyed happiness. This is still taking the words literally and is somewhat forced. Who knew that Chen Shuixiang's public reputation was not as good as his gardener Lu Zhi.

Chen Yengao of the Yuan Dynasty wrote in the Beixuan Notes: "Sima Gong set up the Solitary Garden. In the bright spring, the plants and trees were luxuriant and beautiful. Those who watched all gave money to the gardener Lu Zhi, calling it tea money. He accumulated ten thousand coins and presented them to Gong, but Gong refused, saying, 'Do I lack this?' Zhi said, 'Is it only Duanming in the world who does not love money?' Thereupon, he used all the money to build a parallel pavilion to benefit passersby." Yengao also praised the master and servant, saying: "With only one 'does not love money,' he can be compared to Duanming, and can also awaken Duanming. It is impossible for anyone other than Duanming to have this servant. Unexpectedly, in addition to the talented Junshi, there is such a person." In fact, Duanming had two mistakes: one was that he should not have allowed the gardener to accept money, and the other was that he should not have said that he did not lack it. Fortunately, Lu Zhi was a kind person, not allowing his master to be good alone, but exceeding his master by one step, doing a career of sharing joy with others, and Duanming could not help but feel ashamed.

Originally, "When the prime minister is from Hefei, the world becomes thin; when the agricultural minister is from Changshu, the world becomes barren" has become a common saying. Chen Shuixiang's solitary garden naturally could not escape this common saying. However, he still made some achievements in politics. Although the world became thin, there was still some rice to eat. Although the world became barren, there was still some rice to harvest. Like the current public figures, villas face each other, not allowing idlers, but rather allowing the cobwebs to be sealed. To this day, there are still rubble and debris on the Songhu Road. At that time, I don't know where the displaced refugees went. I heard someone say that last year a certain public figure wanted to send a house to a certain general, but the general said, "Please move this money to build affordable housing for civilians in the capital." This is the poetic idea of Du Fu's "Ten thousand mansions to shelter the poor scholars," but unfortunately these words are most likely to spoil people's fun.

I criticize Chen Shuixiang's public reputation and feel that it is too harsh and unavoidable to blame. Because he still did not want everyone to swallow their tears and shout "Long live the emperor!" There are many public figures in the world who enjoy happiness before anyone else and worry only after everyone else has suffered.

Tavern

— Ying Jun

The northwest wind blew down from the tall western-style buildings on both sides, and my ears seemed to be detaching from my body. Nanjing Road at night, under the rule of the god of winter, was not as lively as in summer. In a dark tavern in the stadium, we skillfully stepped over the threshold.

There was no stove, and the cold still dominated the space. Looking out the glass window on the top floor, the winter sale banners fluttered!

Clams, dried duck gizzards, smoked fish from the old Dafang store. And those wisps of hot air, rising up with blue fish tails and creamed cabbage hearts. These days we have been living in a state of drunkenness. On this night with the northwest wind blowing, I responded to a friend's appointment and still in a distant place, ran over here.

The moment of drunkenness allows us to escape from the cage of worries. After abstaining from alcohol for a year, I am spending my life in a drunken state every day in these nights when my mood is not calm. We are not participating in a grand banquet here, but in a tavern that every petty bourgeois shares. The form of every drunkard squatting at the table is truly exposed. There is no false humility, no symphony of arrogant money. This is where we vent the daily complaints that have been suppressed. The harsh winter of rain and snow has arrived, and the second new year is also passing in a hurry, arriving at the earth struck by the cold wind. When we were children, we always hoped for Lantern Festivals every night. At this time, there were no wounds of life, no sufferings of life. In a lonely foreign land, I thought of my home thousands of miles away, and they were already busy preparing for the New Year. "Wine enters the sorrowful intestines and turns into tears of longing." After drinking, the brain nerves are often filled with some future troubles: this is the so-called "borrowing wine to dispel sorrow only increases sorrow." What's more, for a year, I have been living in a fighting environment.

Plates and wine pots piled up in the corner of the table; my face felt hot. Clam shells and blue fish bones were piled up like small hills in front of everyone. The temperature in the room was also warmer than when I wasn't drunk. Odes to the joys and sorrows of life, we staggered out of the tavern door.

The northwest wind blew down from the tall western-style buildings on both sides, and my ears seemed to be detaching from my body. Nanjing Road at night, under the rule of the god of winter, was not as lively as in summer.

Calendar Posters

— Bo Guang

"Calendar posters are a boon to rural women, they are the most welcome. If it is a newlywed, the four walls of the new house must be covered with 'calendar posters.'" Or at the end of the abandoned lunar year, after sweeping the dust off the furniture in the room, some new "calendar posters" are also hung up.

However, some "calendar posters" are indeed printed very gorgeously, and the women are also beautiful. The products of cigarette companies are the most fashionable. Rural women can only pursue the modern girls in the city on "calendar posters." To make fashionable clothes, they also have to learn the style from "calendar posters." But the "calendar posters" that are popular now do not have the months printed on them. They only print a beautiful woman and their own brand name, which is meaningless. On the contrary, they gradually make frugal women tend to be extravagant. Rather than hanging a meaningless picture, it is better to hang a few war pictures of the "September 18th" or "January 28th" Sino-Japanese War, which can also make the general farmers and rural women aware of China's peril, being bullied by others, and cultivate their patriotic psychology! This kind of hanging picture is much more conscious than calendar posters.

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 24: Sharing Wine and Food in Boisterous Farewell, Burning the Midnight Oil to Relive Dreams, Singing of Longing

Gui Zhi said, "As for me, you don't need to comfort me. It's just Grandpa and my mother, you should talk to them, say a few words of comfort. "Zi Qiang said, "Our grandpa is fine, but you definitely need to comfort your mother. Don't sleep, wait for me, I'll come back." Gui Zhi laughed, "I've even prepared food for you, how could I sleep first?" Reminded by his wife, Zi Qiang couldn't wait for even a moment. He immediately got up and went to the front yard. Today, Mother Yue's attitude had also changed. Seeing her son-in-law, she was full of affection. This made Zi Qiang feel guilty and he couldn't help but continue talking to her. After talking to her, he went to his father's room to talk. When he returned to the newlyweds' room, it was already past twelve o'clock. He saw four small dishes placed there, and Gui Zhi was sitting on a low stool, with her hands pressed on her knees, as if waiting for something. Seeing Zi Qiang, she immediately stepped forward and took his hand, saying, "You've been talking all night, I'm afraid you're hungry, so I prepared a few dishes and noodles for you to eat." Zi Qiang laughed, "Actually, it would be fine if we just sat and chatted for a while, why bother to go to so much trouble?" Gui Zhi smiled, "Judging from today's situation, you are a guest. As the hostess, isn't it my duty to entertain guests?" Zi Qiang laughed, "That's where you're wrong. As the hostess, you should naturally entertain guests, but where is the host?" Gui Zhi pulled him to sit on the stool, lifted the door curtain, peeked outside, then closed the door, opened the cupboard, took out a small bottle of wine, waved it in front of Zi Qiang in the lamplight, and laughed, "Let me secretly have three cups with you." Zi Qiang was barely sober from the alcohol he had already consumed. He didn't want to drink. But since his wife had said so, he couldn't refuse, so he laughed, "What if I get drunk?" Gui Zhi shook the wine bottle a few times and said, "Look at this, it's only four ounces of wine. You have two ounces, I have two ounces. Four ounces of wine, how could it possibly make two people drunk? Let's drink secretly, no one will know." (316)

Winter Protection of Goldfish by Tan Wu Jiren

—

In winter, all animals love warmth, and goldfish are no exception. When cold water freezes, goldfish often freeze to death. However, frozen fish are not necessarily stiff. Try placing frozen fish in warm water and gently heating them with a fire. As the water warms, the fish can gradually revive. Quickly change to well water (freshly drawn) and place them in a separate container in an indoor room. Move them to strong sunlight. When winter ends, place them back in the tank and they will be fine.

In winter, old fish easily turn sideways and lie in the tank. The cause of the illness is no more than two: (1) The tail is injured, with obvious bloodstains, like disharmony of human limbs and meridians, preventing movement; (2) The fish is heavily pregnant with eggs, the belly as big as a drum, causing it to tilt to one side and making it unable to return to its original state when swimming. Therefore, it lies flat with its belly exposed, but it can still eat and excrete, and will be fine in spring.

When adding mud to a yellow sand tank, fill it halfway. In severe cold, hard ice still forms. To prevent problems before they happen, just cover the tank surface with a straw mat every night, and remove it when the sun rises, so that it receives full sunlight. Or, if heavy clouds descend, it is not necessary to remove the straw mat. However, when placing the straw mat on the tank surface, it is best to leave a few inches of space, because even though the climate is cold, the air should still be ventilated.

Brother Yunshu arranged for Wu Yuan to meet Mr. Xu Weishi at a tea gathering. Mr. Weishi told of a method for treating goldfish with white spots and lumps, saying that it had been tried repeatedly without fail. When the problem first arises, quickly take the sick fish out of the tank, take a large inkstone, and use aged ink juice (the ink must be aged, the foreign ink sold in the market these days is of inferior quality, not only ineffective, but also can hasten the death of the fish), drip it into a bowl (the bowl must not have oil). Let the fish bathe in the ink juice for a short time, then take it out and clean it with clear water, and the mold disease can be completely removed, with no problem at all. That is what Weishi said. I have not yet tried it, but he has been raising fish for decades and must not be mistaken. Why don't fellow enthusiasts try it? Previously, I treated moldy fish by shining a strong electric light on them for half a day. The white spots on the fish's body could turn red, and the mold disease could also be eliminated immediately. However, if the electric light shines too hot, the water should also be added or changed. When treating fish, we must be careful in our work. However, compared to Mr. Xu's method, the difficulty is vastly different. Someone might ask, "In Shanghai, where land is worth an ounce of gold, there is definitely no opportunity to raise fish." I say, "That's not true." Mr. Xue Shouling, the manager of Guanshengyuan on the main road, lives in the bustling city, renting a whole building. In the spring, he raised two two-inch-long "dragon egg" goldfish in a foot-wide porcelain basin. During the day, he moved them to sunlight, and in the evening, he left them alone. The fishmonger provided water fleas on a daily basis, and the water was not changed very often, only when it became unbearably dirty. Over the past year, the fish have become fat and large, with bulging bellies. It is expected that they will lay eggs next spring. This refutes the saying that Shanghai people are not suitable for raising fish.

Travel Notes (Continued)

— Chuan Yizhi

If I could have bought a ticket to Lanxi at the riverbank, then I could have spent the night peacefully at an inn in Lanxi, and by noon the next day, the Quzhou-Lanxi bus could have taken me to Qu County. If I could catch the connecting bus, then from Qu County, to Changshan, to Yushan, I could have reached Shangrao on the same day. The Jinhua-Lanxi line is a branch line of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway, opened earlier and with more frequent schedules. Only because I believed someone's words, I had to wait overnight in Jinhua for the train, all the way until noon the next day. This shows how unreliable the trains on the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway are.

In Jinhua, there were no singing girls who squeezed out Peking Opera tunes from their diaphragms, and an old woman, a woman in her fifties, gave us special treatment, inviting my three companions and me to drink tea in the back room of her shop. Inside were three old reclining chairs, next to a large rectangular rice cabinet. Her two young children used the cabinet as their bed, sleeping soundly. Near the door was a coal stove. The old woman, wearing a blue cloth headscarf, added firewood to the stove to boil water. When the water was hot, she first filled the three teacups on a broken square table in front of our reclining chairs, then carried the lead kettle outside to the front shop to refill it. After refilling it, she brought it back in to add water and put it back on the stove to boil. She worked tirelessly like this day and night. Sometimes, she would feel tired and sit by the door to doze off. Her eldest son (I guessed) was a rickshaw puller, because I saw him in the room where we were sitting, tying his long gown tightly with a belt, taking a copper bell, and going out the door to pull his rickshaw. I asked him why he worked so hard day and night to solicit business, and he replied, "To eat." I deeply felt how difficult it was to make a living.

What I found most unforgettable was that she took out one of the thin quilts that her children were using to cover their feet for the three of us, fearing that we would catch a cold lying on the reclining chairs. This kind of Buddhist-like kindness would make any traveler grateful to the point of prostration. However, is it possible to find more such people in this modern society that takes pleasure in destroying lives, which can only occasionally be found among the poor elders in the countryside? But here, the doors were broken and the walls were cracked, and the cold wind took advantage of the gaps to enter, ultimately preventing us from closing our eyes for a nap, and we could not help but fail to live up to her kindness.

Jinhua to Yushan could have been reached on the same day, but because the railway had only recently opened, the route was very unstable, and the train traveled extremely slowly. After crossing Quzhou, the earth was already shrouded in dusk. A soldier on the same train was also going to Yushan. Because Yushan was close to bandit territory, security was extremely tight at night. After twelve o'clock, the pontoon bridge from the station to the street would be raised, and no one was allowed to pass. He did not have the "symbol" (identification), and had already gotten off in Quzhou. There were no hotels near the Yushan station. When the train arrived at Jiangshan, it was already nine o'clock in the evening. In order to avoid sleeping in the open, I also got off at Jiangshan, preparing to take the bus to Guangfeng the next day.

Guangfeng is a tobacco-producing area. Every year, hundreds of "water merchants" buy tobacco leaves and transport them to Shanghai for sale. Now, it is said that this place is also bandit territory. How is the tobacco business? I don't know. The bus speed is three or four times faster than the train on the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway. In less than two hours, it took me to Guangfeng. Although Guangfeng is also bandit territory, the military checks were not strict. I, who did not have a "good citizen certificate" (stamped by the district chief and the fort chief to prove that I was a good citizen, each costing ten or six copper coins), actually entered and left the city in a grand and aboveboard manner. Shangrao was even more troublesome.

I had been away from home for a long time. When I returned home, relatives and friends told me one by one about the "enlightened" rule of the Living阎王 (阎王, a local official's nickname), the "humorous" scolding of people, how the district chief was incorruptible and devoted to public service, the "interesting" beatings when villagers were assigned to build roads, the urgent business of land tax donations, and the conscription of young men. Agencies such as the salt monopoly and the fort office were constantly being established… I was so overwhelmed by what I heard that I couldn't do anything. Although my mother's illness was no longer a concern.
