Reading and a Way Out

— Construction

In school, it truly feels like being in heaven. You don't have to worry about anything, calculate anything. Only when there's no money coming from home do you suffer some temporary poverty. However, that's just temporary, and it doesn't fundamentally affect the issue of eating. Once you're squeezed out of school, it truly feels like falling from the paradise of heaven into the eighteenth level of hell. Things you never had to worry about before, you now have to think about one by one. The comfortable and tranquil life from before seems separated by a layer of curtain, no matter what. What stands in the way is the issue of a job.

Usually receiving an education to become an official, and the mentality of parents wanting their children to become officials, no matter how you say it, is an embarrassing attempt. But people living under this social system can't help but speak this way. I oppose the fundamental spirit of this education. But right now, I can't help but find a way to solve my job problem, because opposition is one issue, and a job is another.

Although it's said that relying on the family at home may allow you to continue to be supported. But it's ultimately just support. And this fundamentally easily leads to alienation in family relationships, and a deep sense of guilt will inevitably arise from this. Why should we fall into such a state?

But when it comes to the job problem, I can't help but be stunned. How can I solve this job problem? I am a student of sociology. What should a student of sociology do?

Because of this kind of question, no matter how much one tries to get rid of it, one can't help but feel anxious. According to general social prejudice, those who have received little education are often high-ranking officials with generous salaries, and those who have muddled through university will be even more comfortable. But the reality is not that easy. The fact is here, it seems that people who have received higher education, specialized education, are the ones who can't find jobs. Does this ironclad evidence mean that society does not need people who have received higher education, or are people who have received higher education not worthy of finding jobs?

The spirit of education is to become an official, but the result of education is that there are no officials to be. It would be fine if there were no officials to be, but not even being able to find a place to eat can't help but make people frustrated. Life is necessary, but where can I find the way out I seek?

The way out for those who study politics is of course to become officials, but the way out for those who study engineering, mechanics, art, literature, commerce, education, and medicine is also to become officials: in the present, even the way out for those who don't study anything is to become officials. Officials are limited, but those who want to be officials are infinite, how will we solve our livelihoods?

Thinking and thinking, it's just trouble again. I've always been troubled non-stop. I've visited countless friends here and there, and they are mostly equally stunned. The threat of unemployment is looming over our heads. Oh, you group of people!

Amateur Mailbox

Unwilling to Marry

Editor:

I have a very difficult matter, and now I especially come to ask for your advice, hoping you can think of a way for me, because I am very troubled by this matter. After you receive this letter, please reply as soon as possible.

When I was a child, my parents arranged a marriage contract with Miss B. In 1932, when I was a little older and had some knowledge, I protested to my parents several times, but they always ignored me. Until the end of last year, my parents suddenly sent what is commonly called "the date" (i.e., the wedding date) to the other party, setting April of this year for me to get married. I am determined not to marry and resolved to dissolve the marriage contract, but my parents are very stubborn and have always been unwilling to dissolve the marriage contract. Also, Miss B's parents and my parents are cousins, and they are often together, so they have a good relationship. I also often meet Miss B, and after several conversations, I feel that Miss B has no learning and her knowledge is very simple. I have asked her to go to school to study, but she ignores me. Now I am determined to dissolve the marriage contract, and although I have not obtained my parents' consent, for the sake of my lifelong happiness, I have to propose it myself. But I am not yet an adult and cannot propose a dissolution. I am preparing to propose this matter directly to Miss B myself, which seems very promising. Is this the right thing to do? Please guide me. Also (after the dissolution), can the other party ask my side for any damages? What attitude should I have towards my parents now? What attitude should I have towards my parents after the dissolution? Finally, I must tell you that I am only nineteen years old and still studying in the second year of high school, and I should not be getting married at all. In short, this is my last struggle, effort, and fight. If I fail, I can only commit suicide. I earnestly ask you to reply to all of the above as soon as possible. I am very grateful.

Respectfully, Li Siqin

Editor's note: Regarding the dissolution of marriage contracts arranged by parents, this mailbox has published a lot. Now, Mr. Li has raised the issue of underage persons dissolving marriage contracts, which should also be discussed.

Marriage and marriage contract are two different things: marriage is the fulfillment of the marriage contract, so not fulfilling the marriage contract arranged by parents, dissolving the marriage contract is certainly a straightforward means, but when this method cannot be used, "not fulfilling the marriage contract"丨 that is, not marrying is also a legitimate and effective method. Because the fulfillment of a marriage contract should depend on whether the marriage contract is legal (Main points of the judgment of the Supreme Court of 19th year, No. 35), and the dissolution of a marriage contract is legally stipulated that it can only be sued for dissolution after reaching adulthood. Moreover, "If one party does not wish to fulfill a marriage contract made by parents for their children, it is legally difficult to force." Therefore, it is not necessary for you to be so anxious to dissolve the marriage contract because the wedding date is approaching. It is fine for you to "not fulfill" it. However, "directly proposing dissolution to Miss B" is a good method, because marriage contracts should be autonomously decided by both parties!

As for the attitude towards your parents, we believe that you do not need to change your face. You should still be the same as before, because being dissatisfied with a marriage contract arranged by parents is not being dissatisfied with parents; moreover, parents arrange marriages for their children out of good intentions, and although we are unwilling to fulfill them, it is absolutely forbidden to harbor resentment. Therefore, after dissolving the contract or not fulfilling the marriage contract, you should sincerely tell your parents your reasons in detail, even if they are not happy, you should not be annoyed.

Damages should be determined by the specific circumstances. According to your situation, there is probably nothing too serious to "claim".

Novel

Husband and Wife (3)

— Yu Mei

"In these two or three years, there have been quite a few bankruptcies in various families."

"Is there a 'grass' radical in it?"

"Although not, it's not far off. Bosses don't dare to do business anymore. Your business is doing well."

"It's not good either. There are too many people, the burden is too heavy, and there's no profit to speak of."

Taking the candy packages wrapped by the young apprentices, and bidding farewell to Zhang Chaofeng, Xu San once again walked onto the street with a lantern, hearing firecrackers going off at the end of the street, crackling and punctuating the atmosphere of this cold Lunar New Year.

The street was quiet; for every person laughing, there were nine sighing. Xu San lowered his head, avoiding stepping into the puddles of melting snow, thinking about how he could turn around his "fate" this year. He also knew that the path to survival was narrow, and that the doors to production and life were closed. Like many others, when he heard about some commander and some commander fighting, he was happy to pay attention to which hero killed the most people. He believed that the coming of the great flood was the will of heaven. He believed that the Japanese attack on Shanhaiguan was predetermined in the "Book of Yin and Yang" five hundred years ago. He believed that everything was destined. But he hoped that he was not destined to be so poor for so long.

He only stretched his neck out when his foot stepped into the gambling house. The atmosphere outside the door was desolate, while inside the door it was lively and noisy. Many people's shadows flickered on the wall, and many voices wove into a swarming vortex.

Su Ba sat on the carpet in his original position. Everyone chatted leisurely, and the light of the opium lamp was a little brighter.

Putting the candy next to the opium tray, listening to Zhao, the accountant, taking his mouth away from the opium pipe and saying "Thank you," Xu San sat behind Su Ba. Putting down the paper bag, Mr. Cao continued the topic from just now, saying,

"Our Guangdong security donation can't be considered small, how come they want to add three strings of cash?"

Su Ba said, "Isn't it because they're jealous? The heat is here with us. One gambling session has to give fifteen strings of cash a day, which is five dollars. One hundred and fifty dollars a month is considered good enough for the Public Security Bureau. It's not a good thing to keep adding like this."

Mr. Cao, with the pipe in his mouth, invited them to take some as well, and everyone agreed, but didn't move.

Changfa, holding his bent knees, said, "The gambling in Hebei Street has reached eighteen strings a day, six dollars!"

Zhao, the accountant, exhaling thick gray smoke from his nostrils and mouth, put down his opium pipe, leaned up, took a sip of tea, picked up a small piece of silver, and said slowly in the light,

"The lamp donation is going to add half a dollar per lamp again, the yamen has been set up again."

"Last time they said they were banning it, alright, three dollars per lamp," Su Ba said, "Now they've officially set up a yamen, so to speak, business is even more difficult."

Xu San didn't say anything, listening to them, thinking about whether he could add two copper coins to the price of opium after the lamp donation increased.

"Who doesn't say that? Now many families are preparing their own. Even stores like Tongtai prepare their own when they invite someone to..." Zhao, the accountant, fell back onto the bed after the last syllable.

Movie Special

Interview with Chinese Film Artists (39) (Continued from yesterday)

— Sha Ji

(10) (6) "Fragrant Grass Beauty" Director Chen Kangran (End)

"After 'Exhibition', what film are you directing now?"

"The film that has already started shooting is 'Woman's Enemy' (title tentative), starring Xu Qinfang, Gao Qianping, and Sun Min. It writes about the pain of women, and also about the crimes of officials. It can probably be finished in March or April."

"What I want to ask now," I said, "is what are your opinions on foreign films?"

"This..." He thought for a long time, remaining silent. Afterwards, he said:

"I think, regarding this point, let me have an opportunity to write it out in writing. I feel like I can't say it all at once right now."

"Alright." I said again, "Then please share some opinions on Chinese films."

He thought for a while again, and then said very carefully:

"Chinese films that can satisfy people are indeed too few, but the path we are currently taking is very correct and obvious. The general audience does not need mythological films or costume dramas. If we are forced to go back to that path, then it will be the decline of Chinese films. Of course, I am not saying that costume dramas should never be filmed. As long as the acting skills are good, they still have a historical meaning. But I personally have never filmed costume dramas, and I will never film that kind of film in the future, just like when I filmed martial arts films in the past. As I said before, it was purely due to capital and starting from a business standpoint. Now the audience is already asking for films that fit their lives and emotions, why should we run backwards?"

"As for us directors, we are under double pressure. It goes without saying about the concessions. We are not allowed to speak, not allowed to express ourselves freely, this is known to everyone. Therefore, we always feel very pitiful about what we express in our works. However, even so, I still hope that film critics will give me strict guidance."

"In addition, what kind of films do you personally think are needed at the moment?"

"I think children's education is the most important. The educational level of Chinese citizens is too low, so we should focus on rural education."

"…………………………"

"Then do you have a side business besides film? How is your daily life?"

"No side business, I often read books and watch movies."

"Don't you write scripts yourself?"

"I used to write, but I don't write anymore."

After that, we talked casually again. I then excused myself and left. (End)

Film Reviews

Review of "Fleeting Years"

— Ling He

丨丨Beijing Screening丨丨

First, I must affirm that this is the most technically perfect work of Tianyi Company.

Although I have never read Zhang Henshui's novel, and I don't know what the original work of "Fleeting Years" is like, in the movie, the sketches of student life are very realistic and vivid in some places. For example, Huang Xishi buys a few candies, carefully puts them in a basin, wraps the teapot in a scarf, and sweeps the garbage in the room and hides it under the bed; these are all unique characteristics of students, especially for waiting for the arrival of a lover, that pure and kind meticulousness of pleasing the lover, are all depicted very delicately in the movie. In addition, there are also passing notes in the classroom, Qiu Jiusi and his like playing finger-guessing games, and singing Peking opera. These are all used by the director as gimmicks, but precisely because of this, they feel lively and real.

I don't care if the original work is so wonderful, but the director Gao Lihen has indeed achieved something valuable in these places. Regarding him, we have seen his "Oppression" (produced by Star) before. In "Oppression", we did not see any special achievements in the director's techniques, but on the contrary, in this "Fleeting Years", he showed his special success.

In addition to the above-mentioned scenes, we might as well talk about the overall aspect. At least we can't find any unreasonable Montage methods. This includes the composition of the picture and the editing of the scenes. Because of his own understanding of student life, because of his experience of petty-bourgeois life, because he is also a figure who escaped from the remnants of feudalism into this transitional era, he created this "Fleeting Years" which is quite close to a realistic portrayal of real life based on his own experience. What is most noteworthy is his grasp of the mood. This should be the most difficult subject in film creation. However, the melancholic and sad, cold tone in "Fleeting Years" is indeed very touching. Based on my own experience, this kind of grasp of atmosphere is not easy to achieve in any department of art. In the movie, Von Stroheim's "Queen Kelly" is undoubtedly the most successful in this aspect. Compared with it, "Fleeting Years" is naturally far inferior, but it is already enough to be touching, especially for our petty-bourgeois group.

Now we might as well list a few more minor points. The good aspects include:

(1) Dissolve of smoke, tea, wine, etc.

(2) The picture of reeds at the beginning is very beautiful. Here, it reminds us of Bai Juyi's poem "Maple leaves and reed flowers rustle in the autumn." If this wonderful poetic meaning can be fully expressed on the screen, how tasteful would that be! Although the director does not have the courage to describe it like this, it is still quite wonderful.

Other insufficient aspects include:

(1) The characters outside Beijing's Qianmen are stiff. This is naturally because it was not filmed in Beijing. But if the director is good at being clever, he can use models instead of photos. If you don't need the characters to come down, isn't it easy to hide?

(2) Many explanatory subtitles can be omitted, such as "The next day at dawn, he got up to sweep the room, waiting for Bai Xingsu to arrive." This is as redundant as "Lonely and desolate night" and "When the lights are bright and the wine is green" in "A Female Star."

(3) Sensual scenes should be strictly criticized.

The above are all about technical reviews. As for the evaluation of the content, the mandarin duck butterfly school is always the mandarin duck butterfly school. Of course, I am not saying that this kind of preaching to young people and teaching that feudal old man to invest in founding a free elementary school is so undesirable, but it is still just a more progressive thing in the mandarin duck butterfly school. As for what we see, it is still behind the times.

Review of "Girl Without a Room"

— Ya Fu

丨Great Light丨

The translated names of foreign films now are really full of strange things. This is not only very far from the original name, but even talking about these four Chinese characters of "Sentimental Lover," it is too vulgar.

Regarding this film, it is obvious that the theme is the ridicule of futurism by realists. Tom is an old realist painter who, after coming to Paris from the United States, is surrounded by new artists, including Russian royalty refugees who have been attacked by revolutionary forces, and wandering musicians and painters. As a result, Tom is influenced by the life and thoughts of this group of artists, and also goes with the flow and becomes a futurist painter. But his works are not understood by the so-called new painters, and some reviewers hang his paintings upside down. From then on, Tom despised this group of so-called artists, but for the sake of eating and selling his paintings for money, he finally gave up his own views and mingled with this group.

From the author's point of view, he is very sorry for the fate of realism. According to his explanation, new art, due to expressionism, constructivism, and even futurism, has become a school, almost forming a trend, and young realists have become incomprehensible followers in order to follow the trend. This seems to be a very shameful phenomenon. But artists still have to eat. Since they cannot change this trend, they have to be assimilated by this trend, which is a very obvious fact.

We know that the emergence of futurism, judging from the initial declaration in 1909, it pushed art from the passivity of the decadent school to omnipotent power, from symbolism to reality, from the past to the future. It is this arrogant abandonment of past art and the pursuit of future art. What they describe are the speeding of cars, the noise of machines in factories, the roar of airplanes, the brilliance of iron bridges, the black smoke of warships, etc. All mechanical materials have become the objects of their art. From this point of view, the emergence of futurism is entirely the praise of and praise for capitalism. In terms of its positive aspects, it naturally abandons all corrupt and decadent things, and praises everything most progressive and most characteristic in the current society. But in the current situation where everything in capitalism is collapsing, what will their inevitable future be? They will have nothing to express, perhaps the final expression in painting will only be black squares.

In the early days of the Five-Year Plan after the Soviet Revolution, there were also futurist paintings praising industry. Therefore, we know that futurism is indeed the most cutting-edge art that reflects the times. Precisely because of this, their progress can become preachers of peace for a new civilization, or they can become revolutionaries for the construction of a new society, and they can also become fascists who are struggling in the old society.

Of course, in this film, the author completely explains and analyzes from the old point of view. He only stubbornly adheres to the existence of old naturalism and ridicules the popular futurism. However, he cannot eliminate the existence of this school, and on the contrary, regrets the demise of realism.

That's right, the author is in an impossible situation. Since he cannot attack head-on, he can only make light-hearted ridicule. Therefore, he not only has the contrast of paintings, but also makes full use of the mockery in their personality or life. The irrationality of the exiles, the decay or slowness of their lives, even more forcefully writes about that group of blind and ignorant appreciators and critics.

He uses a very bright and lively tone, which is naturally very suitable for satire. However, this is by no means an unreasonable disturbance or teasing of a comedy. We don't have to make a special close-up of a fake moon at the beginning to discover his cleverness, let's give another example; if we make a close-up of a landscape painting, we must think it is an outdoor scene, wait a moment, sign Tom's name in the corner, and then move the camera back, so we know that it is a realist oil painting, and the painter's name is Tom, and the protagonist is immediately introduced.

From this we can see that the director Ralph Murphy's technique is indeed very commendable. However, this is by no means a great work, we only feel this lively and delicate animal.

The actors are all acceptable, but Charles Ford is not as profound and moving as in the silent film era.

Movie Novel

Movie Novel Queen Christina (10)

— Watson

Ipa seemed to have nothing to say, only telling her that the Spanish envoy had arrived. Christina's heart leaped with excitement when she heard the name of the Spanish envoy. She tried to hide her feelings, pretending to ask, "What does he look like?" Ipa said, "The Spanish envoy is very young and handsome, and also very extravagant with money. The noble ladies in the court are all infatuated with him." Christina said, "So quickly?" After she finished speaking, an usher came in and said that the Minister of Finance was requesting an audience with Her Majesty. Hearing this, Christina felt the situation become even more tense. She knew that the Minister of Finance, Magnus, was not to be trifled with. He was the most cunning and treacherous minister in the court. Although she herself had no fear of him, it was no longer just her own matter, but concerned the safety and security of another person, so she had to be very careful. After thinking for a moment, she instructed the usher to tell him to wait a while before seeing him. The usher withdrew.

When Christina entered the grand hall, the Minister of Finance, Magnus, immediately turned around. He looked at the Queen wearing the national court dress, which made her appear even more dignified and beautiful, and revealed his admiration. He bent down and kissed the back of the Queen's hand, but the Queen's hand suddenly withdrew. She said that she could not delay any longer, and still had to have an audience with the ministers. Magnus said, "Your Majesty has been away for five days. Where did Your Majesty go? All the ministers in the court are baffled. Did Your Majesty go to Sara?" Christina said, "Perhaps." Magnus said, "But you didn't actually go, because we sent people to look for you." Christina said, "Then I'm fortunate that I didn't go." Magnus's eyes were fixed on the Queen as he asked, "Then why did Your Majesty leave?" Christina said, "To get away for a few days." Magnus said, "To leave me?" Christina said, "To leave all of you a little. You are forcing me to agree. That's why I left to think quietly." Magnus said, "Then have you finished thinking?" Christina said, "I have finished thinking."

(To be continued)

Home
